     <p>The <b>University of California, Los Angeles</b> (<b>UCLA</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">research</a> <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Westwood,_Los_Angeles" title="Westwood, Los Angeles">Westwood</a> neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. It is the second-oldest of the 10 campuses of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-admission_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admission-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA is considered a <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flagship_campus" title="Flagship campus" class="mw-redirect">flagship campus</a> of the UC system, along with <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">UC Berkeley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UCLA_Campus_Profile_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCLA_Campus_Profile-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Times_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Times-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Magazine_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Magazine-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> It offers 337 undergraduate and graduate degree programs in a wide range of disciplines.<sup id="cite_ref-newsroom.ucla.edu_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsroom.ucla.edu-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> With an approximate enrollment of 28,000 undergraduate and 12,000 graduate students, UCLA is the university with the largest enrollment in the state of California<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> and the most popular university in the United States by number of applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university is organized into five undergraduate colleges, seven professional schools, and four professional health science schools. The undergraduate colleges are the College of Letters and Science; Henry Samueli School of Engineering and Applied Science; School of the Arts and Architecture; School of Theater, Film, and Television; and School of Nursing. Fifteen<sup id="cite_ref-NobelFaculty_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NobelFaculty-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NobelAlumni_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NobelAlumni-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> laureates, one <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medalist</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Terence_Tao.2C_.27Mozart_of_Math.2C.27_wins_Fields_Medal.2C_called_.27Nobel_Prize_in_math.27_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Terence_Tao.2C_.27Mozart_of_Math.2C.27_wins_Fields_Medal.2C_called_.27Nobel_Prize_in_math.27-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> and two <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a> winners<sup id="cite_ref-Professor_Judea_Pearl_receives_Alan_Turing_award_for_work_on_artificial_intelligence_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Professor_Judea_Pearl_receives_Alan_Turing_award_for_work_on_artificial_intelligence-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> have been affiliated with the university as faculty, researchers, or alumni. Among the current faculty members, 51 have been elected to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>, 22 to the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>, 37 to the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>, and 120 to the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UCLA_Research_Facts_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCLA_Research_Facts-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UCLA student-athletes compete intercollegiately as the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins" title="UCLA Bruins">Bruins</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a>. The Bruins have won 125 national championships, including 109 <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> team championships, leading the nation as the most successful athletic program.<sup id="cite_ref-NCAA_Rankings_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCAA_Rankings-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UCLA_Champions_Made_Here_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCLA_Champions_Made_Here-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA student-athletes have won 250 <a href="/wiki/Olympic_medals" title="Olympic medals" class="mw-redirect">Olympic medals</a>: 125 gold, 65 silver and 60 bronze.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bruins have competed in every Olympics since 1920 with one exception (1924), and have won a gold medal in every Olympics that the United States has participated in since 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-UCLA_Bruins_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCLA_Bruins-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table id="toc" class="toc">

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="History of the University of California, Los Angeles">History of the University of California, Los Angeles</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In March 1881, after heavy lobbying by Los Angeles residents, the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Legislature" title="California State Legislature">California State Legislature</a> authorized the creation of a southern branch of the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Normal_School" title="California State Normal School">California State Normal School</a> (which later became <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_State_University" title="San Jose State University">San Jose State University</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Los_Angeles" title="Downtown Los Angeles">downtown Los Angeles</a> to train teachers for the growing population of <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. The State <a href="/wiki/Normal_School" title="Normal School" class="mw-redirect">Normal School</a> at Los Angeles opened on August 29, 1882, on what is now the site of the Central Library of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Public_Library" title="Los Angeles Public Library">Los Angeles Public Library</a> system. The new facility included an <a href="/wiki/Elementary_school" title="Elementary school">elementary school</a> where teachers-in-training could practice their teaching technique on children. That elementary school is related to the present day version, <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Lab_School" title="UCLA Lab School">UCLA Lab School</a>. In 1887, the school became known as the Los Angeles State Normal School.<sup id="cite_ref-berkeley_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-berkeley-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA-old-statenormal-campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/UCLA-old-statenormal-campus.jpg/220px-UCLA-old-statenormal-campus.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/UCLA-old-statenormal-campus.jpg/330px-UCLA-old-statenormal-campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/UCLA-old-statenormal-campus.jpg/440px-UCLA-old-statenormal-campus.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA-old-statenormal-campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Los Angeles branch of 
        <a href="/wiki/California_State_Normal_School" title="California State Normal School">California State Normal School</a>, 1881.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1914, the school moved to a new campus on <a href="/wiki/Vermont_Avenue" title="Vermont Avenue">Vermont Avenue</a> (now the site of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_City_College" title="Los Angeles City College">Los Angeles City College</a>) in <a href="/wiki/East_Hollywood,_Los_Angeles" title="East Hollywood, Los Angeles">East Hollywood</a>. In 1917, UC Regent <a href="/w/index.php?title=Edward_Augustus_Dickson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Edward Augustus Dickson (page does not exist)">Edward Augustus Dickson</a>, the only regent representing the Southland at the time, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ernest_Carroll_Moore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ernest Carroll Moore (page does not exist)">Ernest Carroll Moore</a>, Director of the Normal School, began working together to lobby the State Legislature to enable the school to become the second <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> campus, after <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">UC Berkeley</a>. They met resistance from UC Berkeley alumni, Northern California members of the state legislature, and <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Ide_Wheeler" title="Benjamin Ide Wheeler">Benjamin Ide Wheeler</a>, President of the University of California from 1899 to 1919, who were all vigorously opposed to the idea of a southern campus. However, <a href="/wiki/David_Prescott_Barrows" title="David Prescott Barrows">David Prescott Barrows</a>, the new President of the University of California, did not share Wheeler's objections. On May 23, 1919, the Southern Californians' efforts were rewarded when Governor <a href="/wiki/William_Stephens" title="William Stephens">William D. Stephens</a> signed Assembly Bill 626 into law, which merged the Los Angeles Normal School with the University of California as the Southern Branch of the University of California. The same legislation added its general undergraduate program, the College of Letters and Science.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The Southern Branch campus opened on September 15 of that year, offering two-year undergraduate programs to 250 Letters and Science students and 1,250 students in the Teachers College, under Moore's continued direction.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA-vermontcampus-1922.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/UCLA-vermontcampus-1922.jpg/220px-UCLA-vermontcampus-1922.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/UCLA-vermontcampus-1922.jpg/330px-UCLA-vermontcampus-1922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/UCLA-vermontcampus-1922.jpg/440px-UCLA-vermontcampus-1922.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA-vermontcampus-1922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> University of California, Southern Branch's Vermont Campus, 1922.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Under University of California President <a href="/wiki/William_Wallace_Campbell" title="William Wallace Campbell">William Wallace Campbell</a>, enrollment at the Southern Branch expanded so rapidly that by the mid-1920s the institution was outgrowing the 25&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Acre" title="Acre">acre</a> Vermont Avenue location. The Regents conducted a search for a new location and announced their selection of the so-called &quot;Beverly Site&quot;—just west of <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills,_California" title="Beverly Hills, California">Beverly Hills</a>—on March 21, 1925 edging out the panoramic hills of the still-empty Palos Verdes Peninsula. After the athletic teams entered the Pacific Coast conference in 1926, the Southern Branch student council adopted the nickname &quot;Bruins,&quot; a name offered by the student council at UC Berkeley.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1927, the Regents renamed the Southern Branch the &quot;University of California at Los Angeles&quot; (the word &quot;at&quot; was officially replaced by a <a href="/wiki/Comma" title="Comma">comma</a> in 1958, in line with other UC campuses). In the same year, the state broke ground in <a href="/wiki/Westwood,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Westwood, Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Westwood</a> on land sold for $1 million, less than one-third its value, by real estate developers <a href="/wiki/Janss_Investment_Company" title="Janss Investment Company">Edwin and Harold Janss</a>, for whom the Janss Steps are named.<sup id="cite_ref-berkeley_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-berkeley-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The original four buildings were the College Library, <a href="/wiki/Royce_Hall" title="Royce Hall">Royce Hall</a>, the Physics-Biology Building, and the Chemistry Building (now <a href="/wiki/Powell_Library" title="Powell Library">Powell Library</a>, Royce Hall, the Humanities Building, and Haines Hall, respectively), arrayed around a quadrangular courtyard on the 400&nbsp;acre (1.6&nbsp;km&sup2;) campus. The first undergraduate classes on the new campus were held in 1929 with 5,500 students. In 1933, after further lobbying by alumni, faculty, administration and community leaders, UCLA was permitted to award the <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master's degree">master's degree</a>, and in 1936, the <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctorate</a>, against continued resistance from UC Berkeley.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A timeline of the history can be found on its website,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as a published book.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maturity_as_a_university">Maturity as a university</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Maturity as a university">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UCLA was formally elevated to co-equal status with UC Berkeley in 1951, when Raymond B. Allen was named as its first chancellor. Previously, the school's chief executive had been the provost. The appointment of <a href="/wiki/Franklin_David_Murphy" title="Franklin David Murphy">Franklin David Murphy</a> to the position of Chancellor in 1960 helped to spark an era of tremendous growth of facilities and faculty honors. By the end of the decade, UCLA had achieved distinction in a wide range of subjects. This era also secured UCLA's position as a proper university in its own right and not simply a branch of the UC system. This change is exemplified by an incident involving Chancellor Murphy, which was described by him later on:</p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p>&quot;I picked up the telephone and called in from somewhere, and the phone operator said, 'University of California.' And I said, 'Is this Berkeley?' She said, 'No.' I said, 'Well, who have I gotten to?' 'UCLA.' I said, 'Why didn't you say UCLA?' 'Oh,' she said, 'we're instructed to say University of California.' So the next morning I went to the office and wrote a memo; I said, 'Will you please instruct the operators, as of noon today, when they answer the phone to say, &quot;UCLA.&quot;' And they said, 'You know they won't like it at Berkeley.' And I said, 'Well, let's just see. There are a few things maybe we can do around here without getting their permission.'&quot; <sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:220px-UCLA_Bruin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/54/220px-UCLA_Bruin.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:220px-UCLA_Bruin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Bruin statue, designed by Billy Fitzgerald, in Bruin Plaza.
        <sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2006, the university completed Campaign UCLA, which collected over $3.05 billion and is the second most successful fundraising campaign among public universities.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, UCLA raised over $456 million, ranking the institution among the top 10 universities in the United States in total fundraising for the year.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On January 26, 2011, Meyer and Renee Luskin donated $100 million dollars to UCLA.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> On February 14, 2011, UCLA received a $200 million donation gift by The Lincy Foundation in order to establish The Dream Fund, which is &quot;a community-based fund devoted to the support of medical research and academic programs at UCLA.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>When UCLA opened its new campus in 1929, it had four buildings - Royce Hall and Haines Hall on the north, and Powell Library and Kinsey Hall (now the Humanities Building) on the south. The Janss steps were the original 87-step entrance to the university that lead directly to the quad of these four buildings. Today, the campus includes 163 buildings across 419&nbsp;acres (1.7&nbsp;km&sup2;) in the western part of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" title="Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles</a>, north of the <a href="/wiki/Westwood,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Westwood, Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Westwood</a> shopping district and just south of <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Boulevard" title="Sunset Boulevard">Sunset Boulevard</a>. In terms of acreage, it is the second smallest of the ten UC campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-Campus_Facts_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campus_Facts-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus is close but not adjacent to the 405 <a href="/wiki/Interstate_405_(California)" title="Interstate 405 (California)">San Diego Freeway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The campus includes sculpture gardens, fountains, museums, and a mix of architectural styles. It is located in the residential area of <a href="/wiki/Westwood,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Westwood, Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Westwood</a> and bordered by <a href="/wiki/Bel-Air,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Bel-Air, Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Bel-Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills,_California" title="Beverly Hills, California">Beverly Hills</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brentwood,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Brentwood, Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Brentwood</a>. The campus is informally divided into North Campus and South Campus, which are both on the eastern half of the university's land. North Campus is the original campus core; its buildings are more old-fashioned in appearance and clad in imported Italian brick. North Campus is home to the arts, humanities, social sciences, law, and business programs and is centered around ficus and sycamore-lined Dickson Court, also known as the &quot;Sunken Garden.&quot; South Campus is home to the physical sciences, life sciences, engineering, psychology, mathematical sciences, health-related fields, and the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Medical_Center" title="UCLA Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">UCLA Medical Center</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Janss_Steps,_Royce_Hall_in_background,_UCLA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Janss_Steps%2C_Royce_Hall_in_background%2C_UCLA.jpg/220px-Janss_Steps%2C_Royce_Hall_in_background%2C_UCLA.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Janss_Steps%2C_Royce_Hall_in_background%2C_UCLA.jpg/330px-Janss_Steps%2C_Royce_Hall_in_background%2C_UCLA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Janss_Steps%2C_Royce_Hall_in_background%2C_UCLA.jpg/440px-Janss_Steps%2C_Royce_Hall_in_background%2C_UCLA.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Janss_Steps,_Royce_Hall_in_background,_UCLA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Janss Steps, in front of Royce Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Ackerman Union, the <a href="/wiki/John_Wooden" title="John Wooden">John Wooden</a> Center, the <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ashe" title="Arthur Ashe">Arthur Ashe</a> Health and Wellness Center, the Student Activities Center, Kerckhoff Hall, the J.D. Morgan Center, the James West Alumni Center, and <a href="/wiki/Pauley_Pavilion" title="Pauley Pavilion">Pauley Pavilion</a> stand at the center of the campus, bordering Wilson Plaza. Bruin Walk, a heavily traveled pathway from the residential hill to the main campus, bisects the campus.</p> 
     <p>In Wilson Plaza, the Bruin bear serves as a landmark of the UCLA campus that people from all around the world come to take pictures with.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The first campus buildings were designed by the local firm Allison &amp; Allison. The <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_Revival_architecture" title="Romanesque Revival architecture">Romanesque Revival</a> style of these first four structures remained the predominant building style on campus until the 1950s, when architect <a href="/wiki/Welton_Becket" title="Welton Becket">Welton Becket</a> was hired to supervise the expansion of the campus over the next two decades. Becket greatly streamlined the general appearance of the campus, adding several rows of <a href="/wiki/Minimalism" title="Minimalism">minimalist</a>, slab–shaped brick buildings to the southern half of the campus, the largest of these being the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Medical_Center" title="UCLA Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">UCLA Medical Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Architects such as <a href="/wiki/A._Quincy_Jones" title="A. Quincy Jones">A. Quincy Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Pereira" title="William Pereira">William Pereira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Williams_(architect)" title="Paul Williams (architect)">Paul Williams</a> designed many subsequent structures on the campus during the mid-20th century. More recent additions include buildings designed by architects <a href="/wiki/I.M._Pei" title="I.M. Pei" class="mw-redirect">I.M. Pei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venturi,_Scott_Brown_and_Associates" title="Venturi, Scott Brown and Associates" class="mw-redirect">Venturi, Scott Brown and Associates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Meier" title="Richard Meier">Richard Meier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cesar_Pelli" title="Cesar Pelli" class="mw-redirect">Cesar Pelli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Vinoly" title="Rafael Vinoly" class="mw-redirect">Rafael Vinoly</a>. In order to accommodate UCLA's rapidly growing student population, multiple construction and renovation projects are in progress, including expansions of the life sciences and engineering research complexes. This continuous construction gives UCLA the on-campus nickname of &quot;Under Construction Like Always.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-construction_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-construction-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Royce_Hall,_University_of_California,_Los_Angeles_(23-09-2003).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Royce_Hall%2C_University_of_California%2C_Los_Angeles_%2823-09-2003%29.jpg/220px-Royce_Hall%2C_University_of_California%2C_Los_Angeles_%2823-09-2003%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Royce_Hall%2C_University_of_California%2C_Los_Angeles_%2823-09-2003%29.jpg/330px-Royce_Hall%2C_University_of_California%2C_Los_Angeles_%2823-09-2003%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Royce_Hall%2C_University_of_California%2C_Los_Angeles_%2823-09-2003%29.jpg/440px-Royce_Hall%2C_University_of_California%2C_Los_Angeles_%2823-09-2003%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Royce_Hall,_University_of_California,_Los_Angeles_(23-09-2003).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Royce_Hall" title="Royce Hall">Royce Hall</a>, one of the original four buildings, inspired by 
        <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Sant%27Ambrogio" title="Basilica of Sant'Ambrogio">Basilica of Sant'Ambrogio</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The tallest building on campus is named after African-American alumnus <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bunche" title="Ralph Bunche">Ralph Bunche</a>, who received the 1950 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> for negotiating an armistice agreement between the Jews and Arabs in Israel. A bust of him, on the entrance to Bunche Hall, overlooks the <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Murphy" title="Franklin D. Murphy" class="mw-redirect">Franklin D. Murphy</a> Sculpture Garden. He was the first individual of non-European background and the first UCLA alumnus to be honored with the Prize.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Carter_Japanese_Garden" title="Hannah Carter Japanese Garden">Hannah Carter Japanese Garden</a> is located a mile from campus, in the community of <a href="/wiki/Bel_Air,_Los_Angeles" title="Bel Air, Los Angeles">Bel Air</a>. The garden was designed by landscape architect <a href="/wiki/Nagao_Sakurai" title="Nagao Sakurai">Nagao Sakurai</a> of Tokyo and garden designer <a href="/wiki/Kazuo_Nakamura" title="Kazuo Nakamura">Kazuo Nakamura</a> of Kyoto in 1959. After the garden was damaged by heavy rains in 1969, UCLA Professor of Art and Campus Architect Koichi Kawana took on the task of its reconstruction.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>With a location near <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> and a world-famous film and television school, the UCLA campus has attracted filming for decades. Much of the 1985 film <i><a href="/wiki/Gotcha!_(1985_film)" title="Gotcha! (1985 film)">Gotcha!</a></i> was shot at UCLA, as well as <a href="/wiki/John_Singleton" title="John Singleton">John Singleton</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Higher_Learning" title="Higher Learning">Higher Learning</a></i> (1995). <i><a href="/wiki/Legally_Blonde" title="Legally Blonde">Legally Blonde</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/Old_School_(film)" title="Old School (film)">Old School</a></i> (2003), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Nutty_Professor" title="The Nutty Professor">The Nutty Professor</a></i> (1995), <i><a href="/wiki/Erin_Brockovich" title="Erin Brockovich">Erin Brockovich</a></i> (2000), <i><a href="/wiki/How_High" title="How High">How High</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/National_Lampoon%27s_Van_Wilder" title="National Lampoon's Van Wilder">National Lampoon's Van Wilder</a></i> (2002), <i><a href="/wiki/American_Pie_2" title="American Pie 2">American Pie 2</a></i> (2001), and <i><a href="/wiki/Bring_It_On_Again" title="Bring It On Again">Bring It On Again</a></i> (2004) were all mainly shot at the university campus or locale. In January 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/My_Name_is_Khan" title="My Name is Khan" class="mw-redirect">My Name is Khan</a></i> was shot at UCLA. Some of the exterior shots of the fictional UC Sunnydale in <i><a href="/wiki/Buffy_the_Vampire_Slayer_(TV_series)" title="Buffy the Vampire Slayer (TV series)" class="mw-redirect">Buffy the Vampire Slayer</a></i>, and ABC Family original series <a href="/wiki/Greek_(TV_series)" title="Greek (TV series)">Greek</a> were also filmed at UCLA. In response to the major demand for filming, UCLA instated a policy on filming and professional photography at the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> &quot;UCLA is located in Los Angeles, the same place as the American motion picture industry,&quot; said UCLA visiting professor of film and television Jonathan Kuntz.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> &quot;So we're convenient for (almost) all of the movie companies, TV production companies, commercial companies and so on. We're right where the action is.&quot;</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:California_Nanosystems_Institute,_interior_walkways,_UCLA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/California_Nanosystems_Institute%2C_interior_walkways%2C_UCLA.jpg/220px-California_Nanosystems_Institute%2C_interior_walkways%2C_UCLA.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/California_Nanosystems_Institute%2C_interior_walkways%2C_UCLA.jpg/330px-California_Nanosystems_Institute%2C_interior_walkways%2C_UCLA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/California_Nanosystems_Institute%2C_interior_walkways%2C_UCLA.jpg/440px-California_Nanosystems_Institute%2C_interior_walkways%2C_UCLA.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:California_Nanosystems_Institute,_interior_walkways,_UCLA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/California_NanoSystems_Institute" title="California NanoSystems Institute">California NanoSystems Institute</a> interior walkways built over a parking structure.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation_and_parking">Transportation and parking</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Transportation and parking">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The campus maintains 24,000 parking spaces and operates an award-winning sustainable transportation program.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Elements of the sustainable transportation program include vanpools, a campus shuttle system called <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bruinbus.ucla.edu">BruinBus</a>, discounted carpool permits, and subsidized transit passes. One of the pass programs includes BruinGo!,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> which allows students and staff members to purchase discounted one-way or quarterly passes to ride <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California" title="Santa Monica, California">Santa Monica</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Big_Blue_Bus" title="Big Blue Bus">Big Blue Bus</a> and Culver City's <a href="/wiki/Culver_CityBus" title="Culver CityBus">Culver CityBus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Medcenter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/Medcenter.jpg/220px-Medcenter.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/Medcenter.jpg/330px-Medcenter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/43/Medcenter.jpg/440px-Medcenter.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Medcenter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UCLA Medical Plaza, near the main entrance to the campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/David_Geffen_School_of_Medicine_at_UCLA" title="David Geffen School of Medicine at UCLA">David Geffen School of Medicine</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_School_of_Nursing" title="UCLA School of Nursing">School of Nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/UCLA_School_of_Dentistry" title="UCLA School of Dentistry">School of Dentistry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/UCLA_School_of_Public_Health" title="UCLA School of Public Health">Jonathan and Karin Fielding School of Public Health</a>, constitute the professional schools of health science. The <a href="/wiki/California_Nanosystems_Institute" title="California Nanosystems Institute" class="mw-redirect">California NanoSystems Institute</a> is another project that was created out of a partnership with <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara" title="University of California, Santa Barbara">UCSB</a> to pioneer innovations in the field of <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">nanotechnology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-construction_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-construction-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_UCLA_Medical_Center" title="Ronald Reagan UCLA Medical Center">Ronald Reagan UCLA Medical Center</a> is a part of a larger healthcare system, UCLA Health System, which also operates a hospital in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California" title="Santa Monica, California">Santa Monica</a> and twelve primary care clinics throughout <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" title="Los Angeles County" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles County</a>. In addition, the UCLA David Geffen School of Medicine uses two <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" title="Los Angeles County" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles County</a> public hospitals as teaching hospitals—<a href="/wiki/Harbor-UCLA_Medical_Center" title="Harbor-UCLA Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">Harbor-UCLA Medical Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olive_View-UCLA_Medical_Center" title="Olive View-UCLA Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">Olive View-UCLA Medical Center</a>—as well as the largest private nonprofit hospital on the west coast, <a href="/wiki/Cedars-Sinai_Medical_Center" title="Cedars-Sinai Medical Center">Cedars-Sinai Medical Center</a>. In 1981, the UCLA Medical Center made history when an assistant professor named Michael Gottlieb first diagnosed an unknown affliction later to be called <a href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS" class="mw-redirect">AIDS</a>. UCLA medical researchers also pioneered the use of PET scanning to study brain function. The signaling cascade of <a href="/wiki/Nitric_oxide" title="Nitric oxide">nitric oxide</a>, one of the most important molecules in cardiopulmonary physiology was discovered in part by the medical school's Professor of Pharmacology Louis J. Ignarro. For this, he was awarded the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a> along with two other researchers – Robert F. Furchgott of the SUNY Health Science Center and Ferid Murad of the University of Texas Medical School at Houston.</p> 
     <p>In the 2012 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i>, UCLA Medical Center was ranked &quot;Best in the West&quot;, as well as one of the top five hospitals in the United States. In 14 of the 16 medical specialty areas examined, UCLA Medical Center ranked in the top 20.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_rankings">Global rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Global rankings">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>In 2012–2013, UCLA ranked 13th in academics and 8th for reputation in the <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, UCLA was ranked 31st in the <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> 12th in the world (10th in North America) by the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a><sup id="cite_ref-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_-_2012_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities_-_2012-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> and 23rd in the world (13th in North America) in <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a>'</i> Global <a href="/wiki/MBA" title="MBA" class="mw-redirect">MBA</a> Rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Resources_%26_Labor_Review" title="Human Resources &amp; Labor Review" class="mw-redirect">Human Resources &amp; Labor Review</a>, a national human competitiveness index &amp; analysis, ranked the university 14th in the world in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_rankings">National rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: National rankings">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The 2013 annual ranking by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked UCLA second among public universities (tied with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">UVA</a>) and 24th among national universities (tied with UVA and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">USC</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Monthly" title="The Washington Monthly" class="mw-redirect">The Washington Monthly</a></i> ranked UCLA 6th nationally among national universities in 2012, with criteria based on research, community service, and social mobility.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a></i> ranked UCLA 6th out of the top 100 best-value public colleges and universities in the nation, and 1st in California.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA was ranked third among national research universities by the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Princeton Review</i> listed UCLA as a &quot;Dream School&quot; selected by both students and parents in 2010. It was also the only public university in the ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA took the 8th spot among all universities for research spending in the sciences and engineering during the fiscal year 2011, according to a 2012 report by the <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>—UCLA spent $982 million.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_and_professional_schools">Graduate and professional schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Graduate and professional schools">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>UCLA's oldest operating unit, the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Graduate_School_of_Education_and_Information_Studies" title="UCLA Graduate School of Education and Information Studies">Graduate School of Education and Information Studies</a> (GSEIS), was ranked 6th among American graduate schools of education in the 2013 edition of <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report'</i>s &quot;America's Best Graduate Schools&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Other 2013 <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> school rankings include the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Anderson_School_of_Management" title="UCLA Anderson School of Management">Anderson School of Management</a> at #15, the <a href="/wiki/David_Geffen_School_of_Medicine_at_UCLA" title="David Geffen School of Medicine at UCLA">David Geffen School of Medicine</a> at #10 for Primary Care and #13 for Research, the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_School_of_Law" title="UCLA School of Law">School of Law</a> at #15, and the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Henry_Samueli_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Science" title="UCLA Henry Samueli School of Engineering and Applied Science">Henry Samueli School of Engineering and Applied Science</a> at #16; departmental rankings included Clinical Psychology #1, Psychology #3, Fine Arts #4, Geography #4,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Mathematics #8, History #9, Sociology #9, English #10, and Public Health #10.<sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011 <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i> ranked the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_School_of_Nursing" title="UCLA School of Nursing">School of Nursing</a> #21.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, the UCLA School of Theater, Film, and Television was ranked third nationally by <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report</i>,<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and the School of Architecture placed second in the country according to The Key Centre for Architectural Sociology.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Library_system">Library system</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Library system">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles_Library" title="University of California, Los Angeles Library">University of California, Los Angeles Library</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Powell_Library.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Powell_Library.JPG/220px-Powell_Library.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Powell_Library.JPG/330px-Powell_Library.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Powell_Library.JPG/440px-Powell_Library.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Powell_Library.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Powell Library, across the quad from Royce Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UCLA's library system has over eight million books and 70,000 serials spread over twelve libraries and eleven other archives, reading rooms, and research centers. It is the nation's 14th largest library in number of volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The first library, University Library (presently <a href="/wiki/Powell_Library" title="Powell Library">Powell Library</a>), was founded in 1884. In 1910, Elizabeth Fargo became the university's first librarian. <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Clark_Powell" title="Lawrence Clark Powell">Lawrence Powell</a> became librarian in 1944, and began a series of system overhauls and modifications, and in 1959, he was named Dean of the School of Library Service.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> More libraries were added as previous ones filled. Page Ackerman became University Librarian in 1973, and was the nation's first female librarian of a system as large as UCLA's. She oversaw the first coordinations between other UC schools, and formed a new administrative network that is still in use today.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Since her retirement, the system has seen steady growth and improvement under various Librarians. The present University Librarian is Gary E. Strong, who has been in office since September 1, 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate">Undergraduate</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Undergraduate">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div style="float:left;"> 
      <p><big><b>Freshman statistics</b></big><sup id="cite_ref-newsroom.ucla.edu_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsroom.ucla.edu-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-admit_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admit-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     </div> 
     <p>UCLA is rated &quot;Most Selective&quot; by <i>U.S. News &amp; World Report.</i> <sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> It received over 100,000 freshman applications for Fall 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> As of Fall 2013, UCLA is the most selective public university in the United States: it reached a record low admit rate of 20.1%, edging out <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">UC Berkeley</a>'s admit rate of 20.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table class="wikitable sortable" style="width:400px; float:right; margin:10px">

     <p>Just over 3,000 transfer students entered UCLA in Fall 2011, with 92.4% from the <a href="/wiki/California_Community_Colleges_System" title="California Community Colleges System">California Community Colleges System</a>. Over the past 15 years over 45,000 transfer students have entered UCLA. One-third of baccalaureate degrees are awarded to students who entered UCLA as transfer students. One of the major debates is over the decreased admission of <a href="/wiki/African-Americans" title="African-Americans" class="mw-redirect">African-Americans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latinos" title="Latinos" class="mw-redirect">Latinos</a>, especially since the passage of <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_209_(1996)" title="California Proposition 209 (1996)">Proposition 209</a>, prohibiting racial, sexual, or ethnic discrimination at public institutions, in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> In response to this issue, UCLA decided to shift to a more holistic admissions process, similar to that of UC Berkeley, starting Fall 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Preliminary, admitted freshman applicants for Fall 2013 had an average weighted GPA of 4.40 (3.88 unweighted), an average combined SAT score of 2037 (667 for Critical Reading, 690 for Mathematics, and 680 for Writing) and an average ACT Composite score of 30.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate">Graduate</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Graduate">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA_School_of_Law_library_tower_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/UCLA_School_of_Law_library_tower_2.jpg/170px-UCLA_School_of_Law_library_tower_2.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/UCLA_School_of_Law_library_tower_2.jpg/255px-UCLA_School_of_Law_library_tower_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/UCLA_School_of_Law_library_tower_2.jpg/340px-UCLA_School_of_Law_library_tower_2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA_School_of_Law_library_tower_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Hugh and Hazel Darling Law Library, UCLA School of Law
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In Fall 2010, the <a href="/wiki/David_Geffen_School_of_Medicine_at_UCLA" title="David Geffen School of Medicine at UCLA">David Geffen School of Medicine</a> admitted 3.9% of its applicants. In Fall 2011, the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_School_of_Law" title="UCLA School of Law">School of Law</a> admitted 20%. In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Anderson_School_of_Management" title="UCLA Anderson School of Management">Anderson School of Management</a> admitted 22.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to the American Dental Education Association (ADEA) Guide to Dental Schools, 44th Ed., the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_School_of_Dentistry" title="UCLA School of Dentistry">UCLA School of Dentistry</a> had more than 1,465 applicants for 88 seats in the entering class of 2006. The average <a href="/wiki/Dental_Admissions_Test" title="Dental Admissions Test" class="mw-redirect">Dental Admissions Test</a> (DAT) scores for admitted students in the entering class of 2012 were 22 on the academic portion and 21 on the perceptual aptitude portion.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1949 the <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Regents of the University of California</a> authorized the School of Nursing as one of the professional schools of the UCLA Center for the Health Sciences. The Graduate School of Nursing is ranked by U.S. News and World Report as one of the top graduate nursing schools in the country, and currently has an acceptance rate of 3.9%. The school offers professional degrees in Nurse Practitioner, Clinical Nurse Specialist, and Ph.D. in Nursing.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>In 2012, UCLA was rated the most dangerous college campus in the US by <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i> with 921 property crimes, and 49 violent crimes (recorded in the year 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA's director of media relations issued a response to this rank stating crime reports are taken both on and off campus, including the multiple <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" title="Los Angeles County" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles County</a> locations of UCLA medical centers and clinics, suggesting data might be inflated.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Other media outlets, such as the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/LAist" title="LAist" class="mw-redirect">LAist</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/LA_Weekly" title="LA Weekly">LA Weekly</a><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> disputed the ranking.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_impact">Economic impact</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economic impact">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA_hoodie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/UCLA_hoodie.jpg/220px-UCLA_hoodie.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/UCLA_hoodie.jpg/330px-UCLA_hoodie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/UCLA_hoodie.jpg/440px-UCLA_hoodie.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA_hoodie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A 
        <a href="/wiki/Hoodie" title="Hoodie">hoodie</a> from the UCLA Store
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University has a significant impact in the Los Angeles economy. It is the fourth largest employer in the county (after Los Angeles County, the Los Angeles Unified School District and the federal government) and the seventh largest in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trademarks_and_licensing">Trademarks and licensing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Trademarks and licensing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The UCLA trademark &quot;is the exclusive property of the <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Regents of the University of California</a>.&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> but it is managed, protected, and licensed through UCLA Trademarks and Licensing, a division of the Associated Students UCLA.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> As such, the ASUCLA also has a share in the profits.</p> 
     <p>Due to UCLA's academic and athletic prestige, as well as the name being associated with popular images of <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a> lifestyle, apparel with UCLA logos and insignia sells not just in the United States, but as an overseas clothing and accessories brand. High demand for UCLA apparel has inspired the licensing of its trademark to UCLA brand stores throughout Europe, Middle East and Asia. Since 1980, 15 UCLA stores have opened in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and 49 are currently open in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. The newest store was opened in in the Middle East in Kuwait.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> There are also stores in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, India and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stores_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stores-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA makes $400,000 in royalties every year through its international licensing program.<sup id="cite_ref-stores_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stores-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2>
