         <a href="/wiki/File:Drake_Stadium_2008.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Drake Stadium, UCLA's track and field stadium
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA_Bruins_enter_the_LA_Coliseum,_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/UCLA_Bruins_enter_the_LA_Coliseum%2C_2007.jpg/220px-UCLA_Bruins_enter_the_LA_Coliseum%2C_2007.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/UCLA_Bruins_enter_the_LA_Coliseum%2C_2007.jpg/330px-UCLA_Bruins_enter_the_LA_Coliseum%2C_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/UCLA_Bruins_enter_the_LA_Coliseum%2C_2007.jpg/440px-UCLA_Bruins_enter_the_LA_Coliseum%2C_2007.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCLA_Bruins_enter_the_LA_Coliseum,_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UCLA Bruins entering the LA Coliseum in 2007
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The school's sports teams are called the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins" title="UCLA Bruins">Bruins</a>, with colors <a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(color)" title="True Blue (color)">True Blue</a> and gold. The Bruins participate in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I-A</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a>. Two notable sports facilities serve as home venues for UCLA sports. The Bruin men's <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> team plays home games at the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(stadium)" title="Rose Bowl (stadium)">Rose Bowl</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena</a>; the team won a national title in 1954. The men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> and men's and women's <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> teams, and the women's <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnastics</a> team play at <a href="/wiki/Pauley_Pavilion" title="Pauley Pavilion">Pauley Pavilion</a> on campus. The school also sponsors <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer" class="mw-redirect">soccer</a>, women's <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>, and women's <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a>.</p> 
     <p>The Bruin mascots are Joe and Josephine Bruin, and the <a href="/wiki/Fight_songs" title="Fight songs" class="mw-redirect">fight songs</a> are <i><a href="/wiki/Sons_of_Westwood" title="Sons of Westwood">Sons of Westwood</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Mighty_Bruins" title="Mighty Bruins">Mighty Bruins</a></i>. The alma mater is <i><a href="/wiki/Hail_to_the_Hills_of_Westwood" title="Hail to the Hills of Westwood">Hail to the Hills of Westwood</a></i>.</p> 
     <p>When <a href="/wiki/Henry_Russell_Sanders" title="Henry Russell Sanders">Henry &quot;Red&quot; Sanders</a> came to UCLA to coach <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a> in 1949, the uniforms were redesigned. Sanders added a gold loop on the shoulders—the UCLA Stripe. The navy blue was changed to a lighter shade of blue. Sanders figured that the baby blue would look better on the field and in film. He dubbed the baby blue uniform &quot;Powder Keg Blue,&quot; a powder blue with an explosive kick. This would also differentiate UCLA from all other UC teams, as all UC campuses' official colors are blue and gold. UCLA is competitive in all major Division I-A sports and has won 125 national championships, including 109 <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> championships, more than any other university. Most recently, UCLA's <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> team defeated Mississippi State to win its first NCAA National Championship. UCLA's softball program is also outstanding.<sup id="cite_ref-NCAA_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCAA-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Women's softball won their NCAA-leading 11th National Championship, on June 8, 2010. The women's water polo team is also dominant in winning—they won a record 7 NCAA championships. Notably, the team helped UCLA become the first school to win 100 NCAA championships overall when they won their fifth on May 13, 2007.</p> 
     <p>Among these championships, some of the more notable victories are in <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins_men%27s_basketball" title="UCLA Bruins men's basketball">men's basketball</a>. Under legendary coach <a href="/wiki/John_Wooden" title="John Wooden">John Wooden</a>, UCLA men's basketball teams won 10 NCAA championships, including a <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship#Champions.2C_runners-up_and_locations" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">record seven consecutive</a>, in 1964, 1965, 1967, 1968, 1969, 1970, 1971, 1972, 1973, and 1975, and an 11th was added under then-coach Jim Harrick in 1995 (through 2008, the most consecutive by any other team is <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship#Champions.2C_runners-up_and_locations" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">two</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-NCAA_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCAA-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1971 to 1974, UCLA men's basketball won an unprecedented 88 consecutive games. UCLA has also shown dominance in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Volleyball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Volleyball Championship" class="mw-redirect">men's volleyball</a>, with 19 national championships. All 19 teams were led by former<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> coach <a href="/wiki/Al_Scates" title="Al Scates">Al Scates</a>, which ties him with <a href="/wiki/John_McDonnell_(coach)" title="John McDonnell (coach)">John McDonnell</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arkansas" title="University of Arkansas">University of Arkansas</a> as NCAA leader for national championships in a single sport.<sup id="cite_ref-NCAA_107-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCAA-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UCLA has medaled in every <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> they have participated in.</p> 
     <p>Former UCLA <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> player and current <a href="/wiki/Utah_Jazz" title="Utah Jazz">Utah Jazz</a> player <a href="/wiki/Earl_Watson" title="Earl Watson">Earl Watson</a> commented, &quot;Eleven national championships, the best coach (Wooden) to coach the game says a lot. I take offense to those who act like UCLA is just another school compared with <a href="/wiki/Duke_Blue_Devils" title="Duke Blue Devils">Duke</a>. Duke is a great school in the east, but UCLA is worldwide.&quot;</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="USC_rivalry">USC rivalry</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: USC rivalry">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/UCLA-USC_rivalry" title="UCLA-USC rivalry" class="mw-redirect">UCLA-USC rivalry</a>
     </div> 
     <p>UCLA shares a traditional sports rivalry with the nearby <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a>. In football, UCLA has one national champion team and 16 conference titles, compared to USC's 11 national championships and 37 conference championships. Under <a href="/wiki/John_Wooden" title="John Wooden">John Wooden</a>, UCLA became a dominating power in men's basketball, and has won 11 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA championships</a>, against USC's none.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The schools share a rivalry in many other sports. In men's volleyball, UCLA won 19 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Volleyball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Volleyball Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Men's Volleyball Championships</a> against USC's four.<sup id="cite_ref-NCAA_107-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCAA-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA also dominates the all-time series vs. USC in men's volleyball (86–34).<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> In women's volleyball UCLA leads the all-time series against USC as well and has won eight national champions to USC's six.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In the popular sport of soccer UCLA leads USC in the all-time series 13–3–0, yet USC no longer competes in men's NCAA Div 1 soccer.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Lexus_Gauntlet" title="Lexus Gauntlet">Lexus Gauntlet</a> is the name given to the official competition between the two schools in 18 varsity sports where UCLA has won the annual award three times and USC has won the award on eight occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> This rivalry even extends to the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, where UCLA athletes have won 213 medals while USC athletes have won 287.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The origin is unclear, but the rivalry most likely started when football <a href="/wiki/List_of_College_Football_Hall_of_Fame_inductees_(coaches)" title="List of College Football Hall of Fame inductees (coaches)">Hall of Fame coach</a> Red Sanders led UCLA to dominance in the 1950s. USC, having won four national championships prior to UCLA's first and only title in 1954 diverted some attention from then-rival <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">University of Notre Dame</a>, and the new cross-town rivalry began.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> USC has gone on to win 11 National Championships in football.</p> 
     <p>Presently, <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins" title="UCLA Bruins">UCLA</a> has the most NCAA championships, winning a combined 109 team championships in men's and women's sports, with Stanford coming in second with 103, followed by USC with 95.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The campus' location in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" title="Los Angeles, California" class="mw-redirect">Los Angeles</a> makes excursions to local museums, theaters, or other entertainment venues relatively quick and easy. UCLA offers classical <a href="/wiki/Orchestra" title="Orchestra">orchestras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intramural_sports" title="Intramural sports">intramural sports</a>, and over 800 student organizations. UCLA is also home to more than 68 national and local Greek-letter organizations, which collectively constitute the largest membership-based and multi-faceted community on campus. Fraternity and sorority members represent 15% of the student population.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Phrateres" title="Phrateres">Phrateres</a>, a non-exclusive social-service club for women was founded here in 1924 by the Dean of Women, Helen Matthewson Laughlin. Between 1924 and 1967, 23 chapters of Phrateres were installed in schools across North America. The student government at UCLA is the Associated Students UCLA (ASUCLA), governed by a student majority board of directors. It is the umbrella organization that includes the two branches of UCLA's student government, the Graduate Students Association (GSA) and the Undergraduate Students Association Council (USAC), the UCLA Store, the Student Union, Restaurants, Trademark &amp; Licensing, and Student Media (including the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Bruin" title="Daily Bruin">Daily Bruin</a></i>). The Student Alumni Association (SAA), a student-run branch under the UCLA Alumni Association, is responsible for conducting UCLA's oldest and greatest traditions, such as Blue and Gold Week, Senior Send-off, <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Spring_Sing" title="UCLA Spring Sing">Spring Sing</a>, and Dinners for 12 Strangers. UCLA also operates a waterfront facility known as the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://marinaaquaticcenter.org/index.htm">UCLA Marina Aquatic Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Marina_del_Rey" title="Marina del Rey" class="mw-redirect">Marina del Rey</a>. Students and staff participate in dinghy sailing, surfing, windsurfing, rowing, and kayaking.</p> 
     <p>UCLA has an active a cappella student population, with a variety of student organizations across campus. The university is often regarded as the pioneer in the West Coast collegiate contemporary a cappella tradition with its first group, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Awaken_A_Cappella&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Awaken A Cappella (page does not exist)">Awaken A Cappella</a>, founded in 1992. The all-male group on campus, Bruin Harmony, has enjoyed a successful career since its inception in 2006, portraying a collegiate a cappella group in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">The Social Network</a></i> (2010), while the Scattertones have achieved a great deal of success in the <a href="/wiki/International_Championship_of_Collegiate_A_Cappella" title="International Championship of Collegiate A Cappella">International Championship of Collegiate A Cappella</a>, finishing in second-place in 2011. Other a cappella groups on campus include Signature, Random Voices, Medleys, Youthphonics, Deviant Voices, Awechords and Cadenza. YOUTHphonics is UCLA's only nonprofit service-oriented a cappella group focused on youth.</p> 
     <p>There are also a variety of cultural organizations on campus, such as Nikkei Student Union (NSU), Japanese Student Association (JSA),<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Association of Chinese Americans (ACA), Chinese Students Association (CSA), Taiwanese American Union (TAU), Vietnamese Student Union (VSU), Thai Smakom, and Chinese Cultural Dance Club (CCDC), each with its focuses on sharing culture and history. Many of these organizations have an annual &quot;culture night&quot; that usually constitutes drama, traditional dance, modern dance, etc., which raises awareness of culture and history to the campus and community.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university has many traditions and annual events involving students, community, or the city. The school hosts events that usually require participation from more than just the student body, and competitions can occasionally involve celebrity judges and performers.</p> 
     <p>Unicamp, founded in 1934, is UCLA's official charity. It is a week-long summer camp for under-served children from the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_area" title="Greater Los Angeles area" class="mw-redirect">greater Los Angeles area</a>, with UCLA volunteer counselors. Because Unicamp is a non-profit organization, student volunteers from UCLA also fundraise money throughout the year to allow these children to attend summer camp.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>To introduce new students to clubs and activities, UCLA begins the fall quarter with True Bruin Welcome. The week includes the Day of Service for all freshmen, the Enormous Activities Fair, the Sports Fair, and other events. At the end of move-in and the beginning of True Bruin Welcome, UCLA holds Bruin Bash. Hosted by the USAC Campus Events Commission and USAC Cultural Affairs Commission, Bruin Bash includes a concert, dance, and movie. Past performers include <a href="/wiki/Thrice" title="Thrice">Thrice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_(rapper)" title="Common (rapper)" class="mw-redirect">Common</a> in 2005, <a href="/wiki/Xzibit" title="Xzibit">Xzibit</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rooney_(band)" title="Rooney (band)">Rooney</a> in 2006, <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a> in 2007, <a href="/wiki/The_Cool_Kids" title="The Cool Kids">The Cool Kids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estelle_(musician)" title="Estelle (musician)">Estelle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hellogoodbye" title="Hellogoodbye">Hellogoodbye</a> in 2008, <a href="/wiki/LMFAO_(group)" title="LMFAO (group)" class="mw-redirect">LMFAO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clipse" title="Clipse">Clipse</a> in 2009, <a href="/wiki/Ying_Yang_Twins" title="Ying Yang Twins">Ying Yang Twins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Travis_McCoy" title="Travis McCoy" class="mw-redirect">Travis McCoy</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Cataracs" title="The Cataracs">The Cataracs</a> in 2010. Bruin Bash was created as a replacement for Black Sunday, a large-scale day of partying including all fraternities, in North Westwood Village, where the majority of off-campus students reside adjacent to campus.</p> 
     <p>Dance Marathon is an annual event organized by the student group, the Pediatric AIDS Coalition, held in Ackerman Grand Ballroom, where thousands of students raise money and dance to support the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Glaser_Pediatric_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elizabeth Glaser Pediatric AIDS Foundation">Elizabeth Glaser Pediatric AIDS Foundation</a>, Project Kindle, One Heartland, and the UCLA AIDS Institute. Dancers are required to fundraise a minimum amount of $250 before the event, which is a 26-hour <a href="/wiki/Dance_marathon" title="Dance marathon">dance marathon</a>. Dancers are not allowed to sit (except to use the restroom) during the marathon, literally taking a stand against pediatric AIDS, and symbolizing the suffering of children around the world infected with and affected by <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>/<a href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS" class="mw-redirect">AIDS</a>. In 2012, Dance Marathon at UCLA raised a record-breaking $451,000. Since 2002, the Marathon has raised over $3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UCLA students also participate in &quot;Midnight Yell&quot; during finals week, a tradition where every night at midnight (starting on that week's Sunday), students yell as loudly as possible for a few minutes, giving a chance to take a short break from studying and to release some stress.</p> 
     <p>The quarterly <a href="/wiki/Underwear_run" title="Underwear run" class="mw-redirect">Undie Run</a> takes place during the Wednesday evening of Finals Week, when students run through the campus in their underwear or in skimpy costumes. The run first began in Fall of 2001 when a student, Eric Whitehead, wearing what he described as &quot;really short shorts&quot; walked around singing a song and playing a guitar to protest the Police restrictions on the Midnight Yell.<sup id="cite_ref-tradition_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tradition-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> With the increasing safety hazards and Police and Administration involvement, a student committee changed the route in order to satisfy concerns but keep the event. It was changed to a run through campus to the fountain in front of Powell Library, which now culminates with students dancing in the fountain.<sup id="cite_ref-undie_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undie-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> As attendance increased, committees in charge of organizing the event deemed it necessary to employ the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California_Police_Department" title="University of California Police Department">UC Police</a> during the event, to ward off vandalism and dangerous activity.<sup id="cite_ref-undie_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undie-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, the route was changed again to begin at Strathmore and Gayley Avenues instead of Landfair and Gayley Avenues. The Undie Run concept has since spread to other college campuses around the United States, including the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">University of Texas at Austin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University" title="Syracuse University">Syracuse University</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Spring_Sing_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Spring_Sing_2009.jpg/220px-Spring_Sing_2009.jpg" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Spring_Sing_2009.jpg/330px-Spring_Sing_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Spring_Sing_2009.jpg/440px-Spring_Sing_2009.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Spring_Sing_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Spring Sing 2009
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Alumni Association sponsors several events, usually large extravaganzas involving huge amounts of coordination. An example of this is the 60-year old <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Spring_Sing" title="UCLA Spring Sing">Spring Sing</a>, organized by the Student Alumni Association (SAA). Spring Sing is UCLA's oldest tradition—it is an annual gala of student talent, which is held at the Los Angeles Tennis Center on campus. In 2009 the event was held in UCLA's Pauley Pavilion. The committee bestows the George and Ira Gershwin Lifetime Achievement Award each year to a major contributor to the music industry. Past recipients have included <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ella_Fitzgerald" title="Ella Fitzgerald">Ella Fitzgerald</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Taylor" title="James Taylor">James Taylor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ray_Charles" title="Ray Charles">Ray Charles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Cole" title="Natalie Cole">Natalie Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quincy_Jones" title="Quincy Jones">Quincy Jones</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Richie" title="Lionel Richie">Lionel Richie</a>, and in 2009, <a href="/wiki/Julie_Andrews" title="Julie Andrews">Julie Andrews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> The Dinner for 12 Strangers, a common tradition among universities, is a gathering of students, alumni, administration and faculty to network around different interests.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The week before the USC rivalry football game, there is a &quot;Beat 'SC Bonfire and Rally.&quot; The bonfire did not take place in 2006 due to fire hazard issues. Nonetheless, UCLA won the football game, upsetting the #2 ranked Trojans. This led many to believe that dispelling of the tradition led to the victory.</p> 
     <p>The USAC Cultural Affairs Commission hosts the <a href="/wiki/JazzReggae_Festival_@_UCLA" title="JazzReggae Festival @ UCLA">JazzReggae Festival</a>, a two-day concert on <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Day" title="Memorial Day">Memorial Day</a> weekend that attracts more than 20,000 attendees. The JazzReggae Festival is the largest, entirely student produced and run event of its kind on the West Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Kerckhoff_Hall,_UCLA_(2007).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/db/Kerckhoff_Hall%2C_UCLA_%282007%29.jpg/170px-Kerckhoff_Hall%2C_UCLA_%282007%29.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/db/Kerckhoff_Hall%2C_UCLA_%282007%29.jpg/255px-Kerckhoff_Hall%2C_UCLA_%282007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/db/Kerckhoff_Hall%2C_UCLA_%282007%29.jpg/340px-Kerckhoff_Hall%2C_UCLA_%282007%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kerckhoff_Hall,_UCLA_(2007).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Kerckhoff Hall houses the offices of student government and the 
        <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Bruin" title="Daily Bruin">Daily Bruin</a></i>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Associated Students UCLA (ASUCLA) is the official entity encompassing student government and student-led enterprises at UCLA. ASUCLA has four major components: the Undergraduate Students Association, the Graduate Students Association, Student Media, and services &amp; enterprises. However, in common practice, the term ASUCLA is often more narrowly used to refer to the services and enterprises component. This includes the Student Store, Bookstore, Food Services, Student Union, etc. These commercial enterprises serving the UCLA campus community generate approximately $90,000,000 in annual revenues, making it financially the largest student government operation in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> As a nonprofit corporation, the financial goal of ASUCLA is not to maximize return or &quot;profit&quot; but to provide quality services and programs to the campus community at reasonable prices. ASUCLA is governed by a student-majority Board of Directors. The Undergraduate Students Association and Graduate Students Association each appoint three members plus one alternate. In addition to the student members, there are representatives appointed by the administration, the academic senate, and the alumni association. The &quot;services and enterprises&quot; portion of ASUCLA is run by a professional executive director who oversees some 300 professional career staff and 2,000 student employees.</p> 
     <p>The Graduate Students Association is the governing body for approximately 12,000 graduate and professional students at UCLA.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>&quot;USAC&quot; is an acronym for Undergraduate Students Association Council, the governing body of the Undergraduate Students Association (USA) whose membership comprises every UCLA undergraduate student.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> The student body currently has two major political slates, Students First! (established in 1981) and Bruins United (established in 2006).</p> 
     <p>USAC's thirteen student officers and commissioners are elected by members of the Undergraduate Students Association at an annual election held during Spring Quarter. In addition to its thirteen elected members, USAC includes appointed representatives of the Administration, the Alumni, and the Faculty, as well as two ex-officio members, the ASUCLA Executive Director and a student Finance Committee Chairperson who is appointed by the USA President and approved by USAC. All members of USAC may participate fully in Council deliberations, but only the thirteen elected student members have a vote.</p> 
     <p>The thirteen elected positions include: USAC President, Internal Vice President, External Vice President, General Representative (3), Academic Affairs Commissioner, Cultural Affairs Commissioner, Facilities Commissioner, Campus Events Commissioner, Student Welfare Commissioner, Community Service Commissioner, and Financial Supports Commissioner.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The USAC President appoints more than seventy undergraduates to administrative committees and the Academic Affairs Commissioner Appoints approximately 25 undergraduates to Academic Senate Committees. Students have an opportunity to serve on the ASUCLA Board of Directors and the Communications Board, as well as on other significant committees. Through their participation on these campus-wide committees, UCLA undergraduates have had input into the decision making process at a high level.</p> 
     <p>USAC's programs offers additional services to the campus and surrounding communities and provide an opportunity for students to participate in. For example, each year approximately 40,000 students, faculty and staff attend programs of the Campus Events Commission, including a low-cost film program, a speakers program which presents leading figures from a wide range of disciplines, and performances by dozens of entertainers. Two to three thousand UCLA undergraduates participate annually in the more than twenty voluntary outreach programs run by the Community Service Commission. A large corps of undergraduate volunteers also participate in programs run by the Student Welfare Commission, such as AIDS Awareness, Substance Abuse Awareness, Blood Drives and CPR/First Aid Training.</p> 
     <p>Student Media UCLA is the home of UCLA's student-run media, including the campus newspaper, magazines, and radio and television stations.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_publications">Media publications</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Media publications">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Most student media publications distributed on-campus are governed by the ASUCLA Communications Board. The <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Bruin" title="Daily Bruin">Daily Bruin</a></i> is UCLA's most prominent student publication. Founded in 1919 under the name <i>Cub Californian</i>, it has since then developed into <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>' third-most circulated newspaper. It has won over 20 national awards in the last five years, and is regularly commended for layout and content. In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Professional_Journalists" title="Society of Professional Journalists">Society of Professional Journalists</a> awarded it Best All-Around Daily Newspaper in the national Mark of Excellence Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> The newspaper has not been without scrutiny and controversy, and in 1954, the administration attempted to intervene with the previous policy of electing editors by a student council. UCLA Student Media also publishes seven news magazines, each established to serve a special-interest community on campus: <i>Al-Talib</i>, <i>Fem</i>, <i>Ha'Am</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/La_Gente_de_Aztlan" title="La Gente de Aztlan">La Gente de Aztlan</a></i>, <i>Nommo</i>, <i>Pacific Ties</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Outwrite" title="Outwrite" class="mw-redirect">Outwrite</a></i>, a school yearbook, BruinLife, Daily Bruin Television (DBTV), the student-run radio station, <a href="/wiki/UCLAradio.com" title="UCLAradio.com">UCLAradio.com</a>, formerly known as KLA, and the online campus review-site <i>Bruinwalk.com</i>. Student groups such as The Forum for Energy Economics and Development also publish yearly journals focused on energy technologies and industries.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/UCLA_student_housing" title="UCLA student housing">UCLA student housing</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rieber_Terrace,_UCLA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Rieber_Terrace%2C_UCLA.jpg/170px-Rieber_Terrace%2C_UCLA.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Rieber_Terrace%2C_UCLA.jpg/255px-Rieber_Terrace%2C_UCLA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Rieber_Terrace%2C_UCLA.jpg/340px-Rieber_Terrace%2C_UCLA.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rieber_Terrace,_UCLA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Rieber Terrace housing
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UCLA provides housing to over 10,000 undergraduate and 2,900 graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Most undergraduate students are housed in 14 complexes on the western side of campus, referred to by students as &quot;The Hill.&quot; Students can live in halls, plazas, suites, or university apartments, which vary in pricing and privacy. Housing plans also offer students access to dining facilities, which have been ranked by the <i><a href="/wiki/Princeton_Review" title="Princeton Review" class="mw-redirect">Princeton Review</a></i> as some of the best in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> Dining halls are located in De Neve, Rieber, Covel, and Hedrick Halls. In winter 2012, a new dining hall called The Feast at Rieber opened to students.<sup id="cite_ref-din_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-din-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> Residential cafes include Bruin Cafe, Rendezvous, and Cafe 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-din_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-din-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> Cafe 1919's location formerly housed a cafe known as Puzzles.<sup id="cite_ref-din_137-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-din-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA currently offers three years guaranteed housing to its incoming freshman, and one year to incoming transfer students. There are four type of housing available for students, residential halls, deluxe residential halls, residential plazas, and residential suites. Available on the hill are study rooms, basketball courts, tennis courts, and Sunset Recreational Center which includes three pools.</p> 
     <p>Graduate students are housed in one of five apartment complexes. One, Weyburn Terrace, is located just southwest of the campus. The other four are roughly five miles south of UCLA in Palms and Mar Vista. They too vary in pricing and privacy.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Bruin" title="Daily Bruin">Daily Bruin</a></i>, 1,525 beds, 10 faculty in-residence apartments and a 750-seat dining hall will be built on the Northwest Housing Infill Project on the Hill by 2013. The buildings are tentatively titled De Neve Gardenia Way, De Neve Holly Ridge, Sproul Cove, and Sproul Landing.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>If involved in Greek life, students have the option to also live in Greek housing while at UCLA. Oftentimes cheaper than living in the dorms or the apartments, Greek housing is a great option for living arrangements for a year or two. Sorority houses are located on Hilgard Avenue, and the Fraternity houses are placed on the opposite side of campus throughout Westwood Village. A student usually lives with 50+ students in Greek housing.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hospitality">Hospitality</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Hospitality">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Hospitality constituents of the university include departments not directly related to student life or administration. The Hospitality department manages the UCLA Guest House, a full-service, on-campus hotel. The 61-room Guest House services those visiting the university for campus-related activities.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> The department also manages the UCLA Conference Center, a 40&nbsp;acre (0.2&nbsp;km&sup2;) <a href="/wiki/Convention_center" title="Convention center">convention center</a> in the <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino_Mountains" title="San Bernardino Mountains">San Bernardino Mountains</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Arrowhead,_California" title="Lake Arrowhead, California">Lake Arrowhead</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Hospitality also operates UCLA Catering <sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Vending" title="Vending" class="mw-redirect">Vending</a> operation, and summer conference center located on the Westwood campus.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chabad_House">Chabad House</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Chabad House">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The UCLA <a href="/wiki/Chabad_House" title="Chabad House" class="mw-redirect">Chabad House</a> is a community center for <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> students operated by the <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Judaism" title="Orthodox Judaism">Orthodox Jewish</a> <a href="/wiki/Chabad" title="Chabad">Chabad</a> movement. Established in 1969, it was the first Chabad House at a university.<sup id="cite_ref-Chabad.2C_Maya_Balakirsky_Katz_2010.2C_page_152_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chabad.2C_Maya_Balakirsky_Katz_2010.2C_page_152-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1980, three students died in a fire in the original building of the UCLA Chabad House. The present building was erected in their memory. The building, completed in 1984, was the first of many Chabad houses worldwide designed as architectural reproductions of the residence of the Lubavitcher Rebbe, Rabbi <a href="/wiki/Menachem_Mendel_Schneerson" title="Menachem Mendel Schneerson">Menachem Mendel Schneerson</a> at <a href="/wiki/770_Eastern_Parkway" title="770 Eastern Parkway">770 Eastern Parkway</a> in Brooklyn, New York.<sup id="cite_ref-Chabad.2C_Maya_Balakirsky_Katz_2010.2C_page_152_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chabad.2C_Maya_Balakirsky_Katz_2010.2C_page_152-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_and_alumni">Faculty and alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Los_Angeles&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Faculty and alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_California,_Los_Angeles_people" title="List of University of California, Los Angeles people">List of University of California, Los Angeles people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Thirteen Nobel laureates are associated with UCLA: seven professors<sup id="cite_ref-NobelFaculty_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NobelFaculty-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> and six alumni.<sup id="cite_ref-NobelAlumni_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NobelAlumni-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The professors are Lloyd Shapley, Economic Sciences, 2012;<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> Louis Ignarro, Physiology or Medicine, 1998;<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Paul Boyer, Chemistry, 1997;<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Donald Cram, Chemistry, 1987;<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> Julian S. Schwinger, Physics, 1965;<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> and Willard Libby, Chemistry, 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> The alumni Nobel laureates include Richard Heck, Chemistry, 2010;<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> and Elinor Ostrom, Economic Sciences, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> Fifty-two UCLA professors have been awarded <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Fellows" title="Guggenheim Fellows" class="mw-redirect">Guggenheim Fellowships</a>, and eleven are <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows_Program" title="MacArthur Fellows Program">MacArthur Foundation Fellows</a>. Mathematics professor <a href="/wiki/Terence_Tao" title="Terence Tao">Terence Tao</a> was awarded the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hc_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hc-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <p>Geography professor <a href="/wiki/Jared_Diamond" title="Jared Diamond">Jared Diamond</a> won the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> for his book <i><a href="/wiki/Guns,_Germs,_and_Steel" title="Guns, Germs, and Steel">Guns, Germs, and Steel</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Two UCLA history professors have each won 2008 Pulitzer Prizes for general nonfiction and history. <a href="/wiki/Saul_Friedl%C3%A4nder" title="Saul Friedl&auml;nder">Saul Friedl&auml;nder</a>, professor of history and noted scholar of the Nazi Holocaust, won the prize for general nonfiction for his 2006 book, <i>The Years of Extermination: Nazi <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and the Jews, 1939–1945</i>, and Professor Emeritus Daniel Walker Howe won for his 2007 book, <i>What Hath God Wrought: The Transformation of America, 1815–1848</i>.</p> 
     <p>A number of UCLA alumni are notable politicians. In the <a href="/wiki/U.S._House_of_Representatives" title="U.S. House of Representatives" class="mw-redirect">U.S. House of Representatives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Waxman" title="Henry Waxman">Henry Waxman</a> ('61, '64) represents <a href="/wiki/California%27s_30th_congressional_district" title="California's 30th congressional district">California's 30th congressional district</a> and is Chairman of the <a href="/wiki/House_Energy_and_Commerce_Committee" title="House Energy and Commerce Committee" class="mw-redirect">House Energy and Commerce Committee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> U.S. Representative <a href="/wiki/Judy_Chu" title="Judy Chu">Judy Chu</a> ('74) represents <a href="/wiki/California%27s_32nd_congressional_district" title="California's 32nd congressional district">California's 32nd congressional district</a> and became the first <a href="/wiki/Chinese_American" title="Chinese American">Chinese American</a> woman elected to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" title="U.S. Congress" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Congress</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Gillibrand" title="Kirsten Gillibrand">Kirsten Gillibrand</a> ('91) is U.S. Senator from the State of <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a> and former U.S. Representative for <a href="/wiki/New_York%27s_20th_congressional_district" title="New York's 20th congressional district">New York's 20th congressional district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> UCLA boasts two <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Los_Angeles" title="Mayor of Los Angeles">Mayors of Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Bradley_(American_politician)" title="Tom Bradley (American politician)">Tom Bradley</a> (1937-1940), the city's only African-American mayor, and the incumbent, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Villaraigosa" title="Antonio Villaraigosa">Antonio Villaraigosa</a> ('77).</p> 
     <p>Computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Vint_Cerf" title="Vint Cerf">Vint Cerf</a> ('70, '72) is Vice President and Chief Internet Evangelist at <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> and the person most widely considered the &quot;father of the Internet.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Henry_Samueli" title="Henry Samueli">Henry Samueli</a> ('75) is co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Broadcom_Corporation" title="Broadcom Corporation" class="mw-redirect">Broadcom Corporation</a> and owner of the <a href="/wiki/Anaheim_Ducks" title="Anaheim Ducks">Anaheim Ducks</a>.</p> 
     <p>UCLA alumni have also achieved prominence in the arts and entertainment. Composer <a href="/wiki/John_Williams" title="John Williams">John Williams</a> is laureate conductor at the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Pops_Orchestra" title="Boston Pops Orchestra">Boston Pops Orchestra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>-winning composer of the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> film score. <a href="/wiki/Martin_Sherwin" title="Martin Sherwin" class="mw-redirect">Martin Sherwin</a> (’71) was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/American_Prometheus" title="American Prometheus">American Prometheus: The Triumph and Tragedy of J. Robert Oppenheimer</a></i>. Actors <a href="/wiki/Ben_Stiller" title="Ben Stiller">Ben Stiller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Robbins" title="Tim Robbins">Tim Robbins</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">James Franco</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Takei" title="George Takei">George Takei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Astin" title="Sean Astin">Sean Astin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milo_Ventimiglia" title="Milo Ventimiglia">Milo Ventimiglia</a> are also UCLA alumni. Popular music artists <a href="/wiki/Sara_Bareilles" title="Sara Bareilles">Sara Bareilles</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Doors" title="The Doors">The Doors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maroon_5" title="Maroon 5">Maroon 5</a> all attended UCLA. <a href="/wiki/Giada_De_Laurentiis" title="Giada De Laurentiis">Giada De Laurentiis</a> is a program host at <a href="/wiki/Food_Network" title="Food Network">Food Network</a> and former chef at <a href="/wiki/Spago" title="Spago">Spago</a>. <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Bocanegra" title="Carlos Bocanegra">Carlos Bocanegra</a>, the USA soccer team captain is also a UCLA alumnus. <a href="/wiki/Greg_Graffin" title="Greg Graffin">Greg Graffin</a>, lead singer of <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Bad_Religion" title="Bad Religion">Bad Religion</a>, earned a master's degree in Geology at UCLA, and currently teaches a course on evolution there.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UCLA also boasts an excellent military background, with hundreds of alumni moving beyond their undergraduate careers to serve their nation. <a href="/wiki/Carlton_Skinner" title="Carlton Skinner">Carlton Skinner</a> was a U.S. Navy Commander who racially integrated the service at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_2" title="World War 2" class="mw-redirect">World War 2</a> on the <a href="/wiki/USS_Sea_Cloud" title="USS Sea Cloud" class="mw-redirect">USS Sea Cloud</a>. He was also the first civilian governor of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>. <a href="/wiki/Francis_B._Wai" title="Francis B. Wai">Francis B. Wai</a> is, to date, the only Chinese-American and the first Asian-American to be awarded the Congressional <a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor" title="Medal of Honor">Medal of Honor</a> for his actions in World War II. UCLA also lost an alumnus in early 2007 when Second Lieutenant Mark Daily was killed in Mosul, Iraq after his HMMWV was hit by an IED. Lieutenant Daily's service is marked by a plaque located on the northern face of the Student Activities Center (SAC), where the ROTC halls are currently located.</p> 
     <p>UCLA's faculty and alumni have won a number of awards including:</p> 
     <div class="column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 20em; -webkit-column-width: 20em; column-width: 20em;"> 
      <ul> 
       <li>105 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a></li> 
       <li>278 <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Awards</a></li> 
       <li>1 <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a></li> 
       <li>2 <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing awards</a></li> 
       <li>11 <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_Program" title="Fulbright Program">Fulbright Scholars</a> (since 2000)</li>
